<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Hungary.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Hungary.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/16px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png" decoding="async" width="16" height="8" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/24px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Flag_of_Hungary.svg/32px-Flag_of_Hungary.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Portal:Hungary" title="Portal:Hungary">Hungary&#32;portal</a></td></tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-top: 0.6em;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:History_of_Hungary" title="Template:History of Hungary"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:History_of_Hungary" title="Template talk:History of Hungary"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:History_of_Hungary&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Hungarians</b>, also known as <b>Magyars</b> (<a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <i lang="hu">magyarok</i>), are a nation and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> native to <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>: <i lang="hu">Magyarország</i>) and historical Hungarian lands who share a common <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian culture">culture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_history" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian history">history</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">language</a>. Hungarian belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Uralic_languages" title="Uralic languages">Uralic language family</a>. There are an estimated 14.2–14.5 million ethnic Hungarians and their descendants worldwide, of whom 9.6 million live in today's Hungary (as of 2016).<sup id="cite_ref-KSH_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KSH-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> About 2.2 million Hungarians live in areas that were part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> before the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">Treaty of Trianon</a> and are now parts of Hungary's seven neighbouring countries, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Slovakia" title="Hungarians in Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Ukraine" title="Hungarians in Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Romania" title="Hungarians in Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Serbia" title="Hungarians in Serbia">Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_of_Croatia" title="Hungarians of Croatia">Croatia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_diaspora" title="Hungarian diaspora">Slovenia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_diaspora" title="Hungarian diaspora">Austria</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_diaspora" title="Hungarian diaspora">Significant groups</a> of people with Hungarian ancestry live in various other parts of the world, most of them in the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian American">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Canadians" title="Hungarian Canadians">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Germany" title="Hungarians in Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Hungarians in the United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Brazilian" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Brazilian">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Australian">Australia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Argentina" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarians in Argentina">Argentina</a>.
</p><p>Hungarians can be classified into several subgroups according to local linguistic and cultural characteristics; subgroups with distinct identities include the <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9kelys" title="Székelys">Székelys</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Csangos" title="Csangos">Csángós</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%B3c" title="Palóc">Palóc</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Maty%C3%B3" title="Matyó">Matyó</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Jasz_people" title="Jasz people">Jász</a> people, the last being considered to be an originally <a href="/wiki/Iranian_peoples" title="Iranian peoples">Iranic</a> ethnic group being closely related to the <a href="/wiki/Ossetians" title="Ossetians">Ossetians</a> than to other Hungarians.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Hungary" title="Name of Hungary">Name of Hungary</a></div>
<p>The Hungarians' own ethnonym to denote themselves in the Early Middle Ages is uncertain. The <a href="/wiki/Exonym" class="mw-redirect" title="Exonym">exonym</a> "Hungarian" is thought to be derived from Oghur-Turkic <i>On-Ogur</i> (literally "Ten Arrows" or "Ten Tribes"). Another possible explanation comes from the <a href="/wiki/Old_Russian" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Russian">Old Russian</a> "<a href="/wiki/Yugra" title="Yugra">Yugra</a>" ("Югра"). It may refer to the Hungarians during a time when they dwelt east of the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> along the natural borders of Europe and Asia before their conquest of the Carpathian Basin.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Prior to the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_conquest_of_the_Carpathian_Basin" title="Hungarian conquest of the Carpathian Basin">Hungarian conquest of the Carpathian Basin</a> in 895/6 and while they lived on the <a href="/wiki/Etelk%C3%B6z" class="mw-redirect" title="Etelköz">steppes of Eastern Europe</a> east of the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a>, written sources called the Magyars "Hungarians", specifically: "Ungri" by <a href="/wiki/Georgius_Monachus" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgius Monachus">Georgius Monachus</a> in 837, "Ungri" by <i><a href="/wiki/Annales_Bertiniani" title="Annales Bertiniani">Annales Bertiniani</a></i> in 862, and "Ungari" by the <i><a href="/wiki/Annales_ex_Annalibus_Iuvavensibus" class="mw-redirect" title="Annales ex Annalibus Iuvavensibus">Annales ex Annalibus Iuvavensibus</a></i> in 881. The Magyars/Hungarians probably belonged to the Onogur tribal alliance, and it is possible that they became its ethnic majority.<sup id="cite_ref-A_History_of_Hungary_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_History_of_Hungary-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Early_Middle_Ages" title="Early Middle Ages">Early Middle Ages</a>, the Hungarians had many names, including "Węgrzy" (Polish), "Ungherese" (Italian), "Ungar" (German), and "Hungarus".<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The "H-" prefix is a later addition of <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Latin" title="Medieval Latin">Medieval Latin</a>.
</p><p>The Hungarian people refer to themselves by the <a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">demonym</a> "Magyar" rather than "Hungarian".<sup id="cite_ref-A_History_of_Hungary_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A_History_of_Hungary-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> "Magyar" is <a href="/wiki/Finno-Ugric" class="mw-redirect" title="Finno-Ugric">Finno-Ugric</a><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> from the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Hungarian_language" title="History of the Hungarian language">Old Hungarian</a> "mogyër". "Magyar" possibly derived from the name of the most prominent <a href="/wiki/Magyar_tribes" title="Magyar tribes">Hungarian tribe</a>, the "Megyer". The tribal name "Megyer" became "Magyar" in reference to the Hungarian people as a whole.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> "Magyar" may also derive from the <a href="/wiki/Hunnic_language" title="Hunnic language">Hunnic</a> "Muageris" or "<a href="/wiki/Mugel" title="Mugel">Mugel</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> According the Hungarian origin myth <a href="/wiki/Hunor_and_Magor" title="Hunor and Magor">Hunor and Magor</a> (first appeared in the 13th century chronicle <i><a href="/wiki/Gesta_Hunnorum_et_Hungarorum" title="Gesta Hunnorum et Hungarorum">Gesta Hunnorum et Hungarorum</a></i>) the name "Magyar" was given after the legendary forefather, Magor.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The Greek <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">cognate</a> of "<a href="/wiki/Name_of_Turkey#Greek_and_Latin_sources" title="Name of Turkey">Tourkia</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el">Τουρκία</span>) was used by the scholar and <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> <a href="/wiki/Constantine_VII_Porphyrogenitus" class="mw-redirect" title="Constantine VII Porphyrogenitus">Emperor Constantine VII "Porphyrogenitus"</a> in his <i><a href="/wiki/De_Administrando_Imperio" title="De Administrando Imperio">De Administrando Imperio</a></i> of c. AD 950,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PrinzingSalamon1999_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PrinzingSalamon1999-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> though in his use, "Turks" always referred to <a href="/wiki/Magyars" class="mw-redirect" title="Magyars">Magyars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Howorth2008_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Howorth2008-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> This was a misnomer, as while the Magyars had adopted some Turkic cultural traits, they are not a <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic people</a>.
</p><p>The historical Latin phrase "<a href="/wiki/Name_of_Hungary" title="Name of Hungary">Natio Hungarica</a>" ("Hungarian nation") had a wider and political meaning because it once referred to all nobles of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a>, regardless of their ethnicity or mother tongue.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origin">Origin</span></h3>
<p>Recent studies support an origin of the Uralic languages and its speakers, including early Hungarians, in eastern or central <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">Siberia</a>, somewhere between the <a href="/wiki/Ob_River" title="Ob River">Ob</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yenisei_River" title="Yenisei River">Yenisei river</a> or near the <a href="/wiki/Sayan_Mountains" title="Sayan Mountains">Sayan mountains</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>n-<a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a>n borderregion.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> A 2019 study based on genetics, archaeology and linguistics, found that early Uralic speakers arrived from the East, specific from eastern Siberia, and dispersed into several regions North and West.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-4th_century_AD">Pre-4th century AD</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_prehistory" title="Hungarian prehistory">Hungarian prehistory</a></div>
<p>During the 4th millennium BC, the <a href="/wiki/Uralic_languages" title="Uralic languages">Uralic</a>-speaking peoples who were living in the central and southern regions of the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Urals</a> split up. Some dispersed towards the west and northwest and came into contact with <a href="/wiki/Iranian_languages" title="Iranian languages">Iranian speakers</a> who were spreading northwards.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> From at least 2000&#160;BC onwards, the <a href="/wiki/Ugric_languages" title="Ugric languages">Ugrian</a> speakers became distinguished from the rest of the Uralic community, of which the ancestors of the Magyars, being located farther south, were the most numerous. Judging by evidence from burial mounds and settlement sites, they interacted with the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Iranians" title="Indo-Iranians">Indo-Iranian</a> <a href="/wiki/Andronovo_culture" title="Andronovo culture">Andronovo culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Blench_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blench-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="4th_century_to_c._830">4th century to c. 830</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UralMountains1.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/UralMountains1.png/150px-UralMountains1.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="406" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/UralMountains1.png 1.5x" data-file-width="220" data-file-height="596" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UralMountains1.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The possible <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_prehistory#The_Hungarian_Urheimat" title="Hungarian prehistory">homeland of the Hungarians</a>, situated in the Southern Urals.</div></div></div>
<p>In the 4th and 5th centuries&#160;AD, the Hungarians moved from the west of the Ural Mountains to the area between the southern Ural Mountains and the <a href="/wiki/Volga_River" title="Volga River">Volga River</a> known as Bashkiria (<a href="/wiki/Bashkortostan" title="Bashkortostan">Bashkortostan</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Perm_Krai" title="Perm Krai">Perm Krai</a>. In the early 8th century, some of the Hungarians moved to the <a href="/wiki/Don_River,_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Don River, Russia">Don River</a> to an area between the Volga, Don and the <a href="/wiki/Seversky_Donets" class="mw-redirect" title="Seversky Donets">Seversky Donets</a> rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-HungaryEarlyHistory_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HungaryEarlyHistory-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, the descendants of those Hungarians who stayed in <a href="/wiki/Bashkortostan" title="Bashkortostan">Bashkiria</a> remained there as late as 1241.
</p><p>The Hungarians around the Don River were subordinates of the <a href="/wiki/Khazars" title="Khazars">Khazar</a> <a href="/wiki/Khagan" title="Khagan">khaganate</a>. Their neighbours were the archaeological <a href="/wiki/Saltov_Culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Saltov Culture">Saltov Culture</a>, i.e. <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> (Proto-Bulgarians, <a href="/wiki/Onogurs" class="mw-redirect" title="Onogurs">Onogurs</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a>, from whom they learned gardening, elements of cattle breeding and of agriculture. Tradition holds that the Hungarians were organized in a confederacy of seven tribes. The names of the seven tribes were: <i>Jenő</i>, <i>Kér</i>, <i>Keszi</i>, <i>Kürt-Gyarmat</i>, <i>Megyer</i>, <i>Nyék</i>, and <i>Tarján</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="c._830_to_c._895">c. 830 to c. 895</span></h3>
<p>Around 830, a rebellion broke out in the Khazar khaganate. As a result, three <a href="/wiki/Kabar" title="Kabar">Kabar</a> tribes<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> of the Khazars joined the Hungarians and moved to what the Hungarians call the <a href="/wiki/Etelk%C3%B6z" class="mw-redirect" title="Etelköz">Etelköz</a>, the territory between the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathians</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dnieper_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Dnieper River">Dnieper River</a>. The Hungarians faced their first attack by the <a href="/wiki/Pechenegs" title="Pechenegs">Pechenegs</a> around 854,<sup id="cite_ref-HungaryEarlyHistory_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HungaryEarlyHistory-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> though other sources state that an attack by Pechenegs was the reason for their departure to Etelköz. The new neighbours of the Hungarians were the <a href="/wiki/Varangians" title="Varangians">Varangians</a> and the eastern <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>. From 862 onwards, the Hungarians (already referred to as the <i>Ungri</i>) along with their allies, the Kabars, started a series of looting raids from the Etelköz into the Carpathian Basin, mostly against the <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">Eastern Frankish Empire</a> (Germany) and <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravia</a>, but also against the <a href="/wiki/Balaton_principality" class="mw-redirect" title="Balaton principality">Balaton principality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Entering_the_Carpathian_Basin_.28c._895.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Entering_the_Carpathian_Basin_(c._895)">Entering the Carpathian Basin (c. 895)</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_conquest_of_the_Carpathian_Basin" title="Hungarian conquest of the Carpathian Basin">Hungarian conquest of the Carpathian Basin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_basin_before_Hungary" class="mw-redirect" title="Pannonian basin before Hungary">Pannonian basin before Hungary</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Magyarok-Bejovetele-ChroniconPictum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Magyarok-Bejovetele-ChroniconPictum.jpg/220px-Magyarok-Bejovetele-ChroniconPictum.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Magyarok-Bejovetele-ChroniconPictum.jpg/330px-Magyarok-Bejovetele-ChroniconPictum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Magyarok-Bejovetele-ChroniconPictum.jpg/440px-Magyarok-Bejovetele-ChroniconPictum.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1607" data-file-height="1400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Magyarok-Bejovetele-ChroniconPictum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Conquest_of_the_Carpathian_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian Conquest of the Carpathian Basin">Hungarian Conquest of the Carpathian Basin</a>, from the <a href="/wiki/Chronicon_Pictum" title="Chronicon Pictum">Chronicon Pictum</a>, 1360.</div></div></div>
<p>In 895/896, under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/%C3%81rp%C3%A1d" title="Árpád">Árpád</a>, some Hungarians crossed the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathians</a> and entered the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Carpathian Basin">Carpathian Basin</a>. The tribe called Magyar was the leading tribe of the Hungarian alliance that conquered the centre of the basin. At the same time (c. 895), due to their involvement in the 894–896 <a href="/wiki/Byzantine%E2%80%93Bulgarian_wars" title="Byzantine–Bulgarian wars">Bulgaro-Byzantine war</a>, Hungarians in Etelköz were attacked by Bulgaria and then by their old enemies the Pechenegs. The <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a> won the decisive <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Southern_Buh" title="Battle of Southern Buh">battle of Southern Buh</a>. It is uncertain whether or not those conflicts were the cause of the Hungarian departure from Etelköz.
</p><p>From the upper <a href="/wiki/Tisza" title="Tisza">Tisza</a> region of the Carpathian Basin, the Hungarians intensified their looting raids across continental Europe. In 900, they moved from the upper Tisza river to Transdanubia (<a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">Pannonia</a>),<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> which later became the core of the arising Hungarian state. At the time of the Hungarian migration, the land was inhabited only by a sparse population of Slavs, numbering about 200,000,<sup id="cite_ref-HungaryEarlyHistory_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HungaryEarlyHistory-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> who were either assimilated or enslaved by the Hungarians.<sup id="cite_ref-HungaryEarlyHistory_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HungaryEarlyHistory-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Archaeological findings (e.g. in the <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Polish</a> city of <a href="/wiki/Przemy%C5%9Bl" title="Przemyśl">Przemyśl</a>) suggest that many Hungarians remained to the north of the Carpathians after 895/896.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> There is also a consistent Hungarian population in <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9kelys" title="Székelys">Székelys</a>, who comprise 40% of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Romania" title="Hungarians in Romania">Hungarians in Romania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The Székely people's origin, and in particular the time of their settlement in Transylvania, is a matter of historical controversy.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="After_900">After 900</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_invasions_of_Europe" title="Hungarian invasions of Europe">Hungarian invasions of Europe</a></div>
<p>In 907, the Hungarians destroyed a <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">Bavarian</a> army in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pressburg" title="Battle of Pressburg">Battle of Pressburg</a> and laid the territories of present-day Germany, France, and Italy open to Hungarian raids, which were fast and devastating. The Hungarians defeated the Imperial Army of <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Child" title="Louis the Child">Louis the Child</a>, son of <a href="/wiki/Arnulf_of_Carinthia" title="Arnulf of Carinthia">Arnulf of Carinthia</a> and last legitimate descendant of the German branch of the house of <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a> in 910. From 917 to 925, Hungarians raided through <a href="/wiki/Basle" class="mw-redirect" title="Basle">Basle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alsace" title="Alsace">Alsace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burgundy_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Burgundy (region)">Burgundy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">Saxony</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Provence" title="Provence">Provence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Hungarian expansion was checked at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lechfeld" title="Battle of Lechfeld">Battle of Lechfeld</a> in 955, ending their raids against <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>, but raids on the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Balkan Peninsula">Balkan Peninsula</a> continued until 970.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a> approved Hungarian settlement in the area when their leaders converted to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_I_of_Hungary" title="Stephen I of Hungary">St. King Stephen I</a> (<i>Szent István</i>) was crowned King of Hungary in 1001. The century between the arrival of the Hungarians from the eastern European plains and the consolidation of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> in 1001 was dominated by pillaging campaigns across Europe, from Dania (<a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>) to the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> (contemporary Spain and Portugal).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> After the acceptance of the nation into Christian Europe under Stephen I, Hungary served as a bulwark against further invasions from the east and south, especially by the Turks.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Magyars_900-1980.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Magyars_900-1980.png/220px-Magyars_900-1980.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Magyars_900-1980.png/330px-Magyars_900-1980.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Magyars_900-1980.png/440px-Magyars_900-1980.png 2x" data-file-width="970" data-file-height="604" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Magyars_900-1980.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Population growth of Hungarians (900–1980)</div></div></div>
<p>At this time, the Hungarian nation numbered around 400,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-HungaryEarlyHistory_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HungaryEarlyHistory-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period_to_present">Early modern period to present</span></h3>
<p>The first accurate measurements of the population of the Kingdom of Hungary including ethnic composition were carried out in 1850–51. There is a debate among Hungarian and non-Hungarian (especially <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanian</a>) historians about the possible changes in the ethnic structure of the region throughout history. Some historians support the theory that the proportion of Hungarians in the Carpathian Basin was at an almost constant 80% during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica2_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica2-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hungary_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hungary-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-boundary_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boundary-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-carth_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carth-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steven_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steven-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Non-Hungarians numbered hardly more than 20% to 25% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica2_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica2-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The Hungarian population began to decrease only at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> conquest,<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica2_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica2-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hungary_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hungary-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steven_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steven-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> reaching as low as around 39% by the end of the 18th century. The decline of the Hungarians was due to the constant wars, Ottoman raids, famines, and plagues during the 150 years of Ottoman rule.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica2_40-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica2-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hungary_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hungary-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steven_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steven-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The main zones of war were the territories inhabited by the Hungarians, so the death toll depleted them at a much higher rate than among other nationalities.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica2_40-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica2-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steven_44-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steven-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In the 18th century, their proportion declined further because of the influx of new settlers from Europe, especially Slovaks, <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">Serbs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Macartney1962_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macartney1962-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> As a consequence of Turkish occupation and Habsburg colonization policies, the country underwent a great change in ethnic composition as its population more than tripled to 8 million between 1720 and 1787, while only 39% of its people were Hungarians, who lived primarily in the centre of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica2_40-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica2-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hungary_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hungary-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-boundary_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boundary-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Steven_44-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Steven-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dunamenti_viseletek_1822.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Dunamenti_viseletek_1822.jpg/170px-Dunamenti_viseletek_1822.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Dunamenti_viseletek_1822.jpg/255px-Dunamenti_viseletek_1822.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Dunamenti_viseletek_1822.jpg/340px-Dunamenti_viseletek_1822.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1451" data-file-height="1954" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dunamenti_viseletek_1822.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional Hungarian costumes, 1822</div></div></div>
<p>Other historians, particularly Slovaks and Romanians, argue that the drastic change in the ethnic structure hypothesized by Hungarian historians in fact did not occur. They argue that the Hungarians accounted for only about 30–40%<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> of the Kingdom's population from its establishment. In particular, there is a <a href="/wiki/Origin_of_the_Romanians" title="Origin of the Romanians">fierce debate</a> among Hungarians and Romanian historians about the ethnic composition of <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a> through these times.
</p><p>In the 19th century, the proportion of Hungarians in the Kingdom of Hungary rose gradually, reaching over 50% by 1900 due to higher natural growth and <a href="/wiki/Magyarization" title="Magyarization">Magyarization</a>. Between 1787 and 1910 the number of ethnic Hungarians rose from 2.3 million to 10.2 million, accompanied by the resettlement of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Hungarian_Plain" title="Great Hungarian Plain">Great Hungarian Plain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Voivodina" class="mw-redirect" title="Voivodina">Voivodina</a> by mainly <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> Hungarian settlers from the northern and western counties of the Kingdom of Hungary. In 1715 (after the Ottoman occupation), the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Great_Plain" title="Southern Great Plain">Southern Great Plain</a> was nearly uninhabited but now has 1.3 million inhabitants, nearly all of them Hungarians.
</p><p>Spontaneous assimilation was an important factor, especially among the German and Jewish minorities and the citizens of the bigger towns. On the other hand, about 1.5 million people (about two-thirds non-Hungarian) left the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Kingdom of Hungary</a> between 1890–1910 to escape from <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poverty</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-immigrants_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immigrants-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hungarians_in_Hungary_(1890).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Hungarians_in_Hungary_%281890%29.png/220px-Hungarians_in_Hungary_%281890%29.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Hungarians_in_Hungary_%281890%29.png/330px-Hungarians_in_Hungary_%281890%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Hungarians_in_Hungary_%281890%29.png/440px-Hungarians_in_Hungary_%281890%29.png 2x" data-file-width="1064" data-file-height="766" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hungarians_in_Hungary_(1890).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Magyars (Hungarians) in Hungary, 1890 census</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Magyarorszag_1920.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Magyarorszag_1920.png/220px-Magyarorszag_1920.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Magyarorszag_1920.png/330px-Magyarorszag_1920.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Magyarorszag_1920.png/440px-Magyarorszag_1920.png 2x" data-file-width="1140" data-file-height="774" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Magyarorszag_1920.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">Treaty of Trianon</a>: Kingdom of Hungary lost 72% of its land and 3.3 million people of Hungarian ethnicity.</div></div></div>
<p>The years 1918 to 1920 were a turning point in the Hungarians' history. By the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">Treaty of Trianon</a>, the Kingdom had been cut into several parts, leaving only a quarter of its original size. One-third of the Hungarians became minorities in the neighbouring countries.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> During the remainder of the 20th century, the Hungarians population of Hungary grew from 7.1 million (1920) to around 10.4 million (1980), despite losses during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a> and the wave of emigration after the attempted <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_revolution_of_1956" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian revolution of 1956">revolution in 1956</a>. The number of Hungarians in the neighbouring countries tended to remain the same or slightly decreased, mostly due to assimilation (sometimes forced; see <a href="/wiki/Slovakization" title="Slovakization">Slovakization</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romanianization" title="Romanianization">Romanianization</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kovrig_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kovrig-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and to emigration to Hungary (in the 1990s, especially from <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a>).
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Post-World_War_II_baby_boom" class="mw-redirect" title="Post-World War II baby boom">"baby boom" of the 1950s</a> (<i>Ratkó era</i>), a serious demographic crisis began to develop in Hungary and its neighbours.<sup id="cite_ref-origo_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-origo-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The Hungarian population reached its maximum in 1980, then began to decline.<sup id="cite_ref-origo_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-origo-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For historical reasons (see <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">Treaty of Trianon</a>), significant Hungarian minority populations can be found in the surrounding countries, most of them in <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_minority_in_Romania" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarian minority in Romania">Romania</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>), <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Slovakia" title="Hungarians in Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Vojvodina" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarians in Vojvodina">Serbia</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a>). Sizable minorities live also in <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Ukraine" title="Hungarians in Ukraine">Ukraine</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Ruthenia" title="Carpathian Ruthenia">Transcarpathia</a>), <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Croatia" class="mw-redirect" title="Hungarians in Croatia">Croatia</a> (primarily <a href="/wiki/Slavonia" title="Slavonia">Slavonia</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Austria" title="Hungarians in Austria">Austria</a> (in <a href="/wiki/Burgenland" title="Burgenland">Burgenland</a>). Slovenia is also host to a number of ethnic Hungarians, and Hungarian language has an official status in parts of the <a href="/wiki/Prekmurje" title="Prekmurje">Prekmurje</a> region. Today more than two million ethnic Hungarians live in nearby countries.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There was a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> in Hungary in December 2004 on whether to grant Hungarian <a href="/wiki/Citizenship" title="Citizenship">citizenship</a> to Hungarians living outside Hungary's borders (i.e. without requiring a permanent residence in Hungary). The referendum failed due to insufficient <a href="/wiki/Voter_turnout" title="Voter turnout">voter turnout</a>. On 26 May 2010, Hungary's Parliament passed a bill granting dual citizenship to ethnic Hungarians living outside of Hungary. Some neighboring countries with sizable Hungarian minorities expressed concerns over the legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_affiliations_and_genetic_origins">Ethnic affiliations and genetic origins</span></h2>
<table class="box-Overly_detailed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-overly_detailed" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>may contain an excessive amount of intricate detail that may interest only a particular audience</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help by <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Content_forking#Article_spinoffs:_.22Summary_style.22_meta-articles_and_summary_sections" title="Wikipedia:Content forking">spinning off</a> or <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Handling_trivia#Recommendations_for_handling_trivia" title="Wikipedia:Handling trivia">relocating</a> any relevant information, and removing excessive detail that may be against <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:What_Wikipedia_is_not" title="Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not">Wikipedia's inclusion policy</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">September 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Origin_of_Hungarians_according_to_Kinga_Ery.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Origin_of_Hungarians_according_to_Kinga_Ery.png/220px-Origin_of_Hungarians_according_to_Kinga_Ery.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Origin_of_Hungarians_according_to_Kinga_Ery.png/330px-Origin_of_Hungarians_according_to_Kinga_Ery.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d3/Origin_of_Hungarians_according_to_Kinga_Ery.png 2x" data-file-width="423" data-file-height="392" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Origin_of_Hungarians_according_to_Kinga_Ery.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The place of origin for the regional groups of Hungarians in the conquest period according to Kinga Éry</div></div></div>
<p>Thanks to <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1l_Lipt%C3%A1k" title="Pál Lipták">Pál Lipták</a>'s research it has been known for almost half a century that only 16.7 percent of 10th-century human bones belong to the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_(mixed_ancestry)" title="Eurasian (mixed ancestry)">Euro-Mongoloid</a> and Mongoloid types.<sup id="cite_ref-Bálint_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bálint-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The European characteristics in the biological composition of the recent Hungarian population and the lack of Asian markers are not solely due to the thousand years of blending.<sup id="cite_ref-Bálint_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bálint-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The population around 1000 AD in Hungary was made up almost exclusively of people who were genetically <a href="/wiki/Caucasian_race" title="Caucasian race">Europid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bálint_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bálint-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a 2008 publication from the <a href="/wiki/European_Journal_of_Human_Genetics" title="European Journal of Human Genetics">European Journal of Human Genetics</a>, the Y-DNA haplogroup <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_R1a" title="Haplogroup R1a">Haplogroup R1a1a-M17</a> was found amongst 57% of modern Hungarian male samples, genetically clustering them with that of their neighboring <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavic</a> neighbors, the <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czechs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">Poles</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">Slovaks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Another study on <a href="/wiki/Y-Chromosome" class="mw-redirect" title="Y-Chromosome">Y-Chromosome</a> markers concluded that "modern Hungarian and <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9kelys" title="Székelys">Székelys</a> (a subgroup of Hungarians living in the <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9kely_Land" title="Székely Land">Székely Land</a> in modern-day central Romania) are genetically related, and that they share similar components described for other Europeans, except for the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_P_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup P (Y-DNA)">Haplogroup P (M173)</a> in Székely samples, which may reflect a <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Asian">Central Asian</a> connection from the time of the Hungarian migration from the Urals to Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-CsányiBogácsi-Szabó20082_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CsányiBogácsi-Szabó20082-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Recent genetic research is in line with the previous archaeological and anthropological assumptions that the original Hungarian conqueror tribes were related to the Onogur-Bulgars.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_Szeged_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_Szeged-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> A substantial part of the conquerors show similarities to the <a href="/wiki/Xiongnu" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a> and Asian Scythians and presumably this Inner Asian component on their way to Europe mixed with the peoples of the Pontic steppes. According to this study the conqueror Hungarians owned their mostly Europid characteristics to the descendants of the <a href="/wiki/Srubnaya_culture" title="Srubnaya culture">Srubnaya culture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2018_Szeged_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2018_Szeged-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Neparáczki argues, based on new archeogenetic results, that the Conqueror Hungarians were mostly a mixture of Hunnic, Slavic, and Germanic tribes having comparable proportion of European and Asian origin and this composite people evolved in the steppes of Eastern Europe between 400 and 1000 AD.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> His research group also established that "genetic continuity can be detected between ancient and modern Hungarians"<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> and "genetic heritage of the Conquerors definitely persists in modern Hungarians" in almost 1/8th of recent Hungarian gene pool.<sup id="cite_ref-Neparaczki_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neparaczki-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> According to Neparáczki: "From all recent and archaic populations tested the <a href="/wiki/Volga_Tatars" title="Volga Tatars">Volga Tatars</a> show the smallest genetic distance to the entire Conqueror population" and "a direct genetic relation of the Conquerors to <a href="/wiki/Onogurs" class="mw-redirect" title="Onogurs">Onogur</a>-<a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgar</a> ancestors of these groups is very feasible."<sup id="cite_ref-Neparaczki_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neparaczki-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another study on <a href="/wiki/Y-Chromosome" class="mw-redirect" title="Y-Chromosome">Y-Chromosome</a> markers concluded that "modern Hungarian and <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9kelys" title="Székelys">Székely</a> populations are genetically closely related", and that they "share similar components described for other Europeans, except for the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_P_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup P (Y-DNA)">haplogroup P</a>*(xM173) in Székely samples, which may reflect a <a href="/wiki/Central_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Asian">Central Asian</a> connection, and high frequency of <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_J_(Y-DNA)" title="Haplogroup J (Y-DNA)">haplogroup J</a> in both Székelys and Hungarians".<sup id="cite_ref-CsányiBogácsi-Szabó2008_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CsányiBogácsi-Szabó2008-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The subclade of Haplogroup N, which is N-L1034 and a Uralic link, is shared by 4% of the Székely Hungarians and 15% of the closest language relatives the <a href="/wiki/Mansis" class="mw-redirect" title="Mansis">Mansis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Neparaczki_62-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Neparaczki-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A 2007 study on the <a href="/wiki/MtDNA" class="mw-redirect" title="MtDNA">mtDNA</a>, after precising that "Hungarians are unique among the other European populations because according to history the ancient <a href="/wiki/Magyars" class="mw-redirect" title="Magyars">Magyars</a> had come from the eastern side of the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> and settled down in the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Carpathian basin">Carpathian basin</a> in the 9th century AD", shows that the <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_M_(mtDNA)" title="Haplogroup M (mtDNA)">haplogroup M</a>, "characteristic mainly for Asian populations", is "found in approximately 5% of the total", which thus "suggests that an Asian matrilineal ancestry, even if in a small incidence, can be detected among modern Hungarians."<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a 2008 study, the mitochondrial lines of the modern Hungarians are indistinct from that of neighbouring <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavs</a>, but they are distinct from that of the ancient Hungarians (Magyars). Four 10th century skeletons from well documented cemeteries in Hungary of ancient <a href="/wiki/Magyar_tribes" title="Magyar tribes">Magyar</a> individuals were sampled.<sup id="cite_ref-csanyi_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csanyi-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Two of the four males belonged to Y-DNA <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_N-M231" title="Haplogroup N-M231">Haplogroup N</a> confirming their Uralic origin. None out of 100 sampled modern Hungarians carried the haplogroup, and just one of about 94 <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9kelys" title="Székelys">Székelys</a> carried it. The study also stated that it was possible that the more numerous pre-existing populations or substantional later migrations, mostly Avars and <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a>, accepted the Uralic language of the elite.<sup id="cite_ref-csanyi_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csanyi-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An <a href="/wiki/Autosomal" class="mw-redirect" title="Autosomal">autosomal</a> analysis,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> studying non-European admixture in Europeans, found 4.4% of admixture of non-European and non-Middle Eastern origin among Hungarians, which was the strongest among sampled populations. It was found at 3.6% in Belarusians, 2.5% in Romanians, 2.3% in Bulgarians and Lithuanians, 1.9% in Poles and 0% in Greeks. The authors stated "This signal might correspond to a small genetic legacy from invasions of peoples from the Asian steppes (e.g., the Huns, Magyars, and Bulgars) during the first millennium CE.".
</p><p>Compared to the European nations, Andrea Vágó-Zalán's study determined that the Bulgarians were genetically the closest and the Estonians and Finns were among the furthest from the recent Hungarian population.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Anthropologically, the type of Magyars of the conquest phase shows similarities with modern Central Asians. The "<i>Turanid</i>" (South-Siberian) and the "<i>Uralid</i>" types from the <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_(mixed_ancestry)" title="Eurasian (mixed ancestry)">Europid-Mongoloid admixture</a> were dominant among the conquering Hungarians.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A recent study from 2018 shows that ancient samples of both Magyars and Avars can clearly be linked to several <a href="/wiki/Mongoloid" title="Mongoloid">Mongoloid</a> groups of East Asia and Siberia. The samples are most closely related to populations in modern <a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_China" title="North China">Northern China</a>. The scientists suggest that modern groups like <a href="/wiki/Yakuts" title="Yakuts">Yakuts</a> or <a href="/wiki/Tungusic_peoples" title="Tungusic peoples">Tungusic peoples</a> share a close relation to ancient Hungarians and Avars.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paternal_haplogroups">Paternal haplogroups</span></h3>
<p>According to Pamjav Horolma's study, which is based on 230 samples and expected to include 6-8% <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Gypsy peoples</a>, the small Hungarian haplogroup distribution study from Hungary is as follows: 26% R1a, 20% I2a, 19% R1b, 7% I, 6% J2, 5% H, 5% G2a, 5% E1b1b1a1, 3% J1, &lt;1% N, &lt;1% R2.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> According to another study by Pamjav, the area of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bodrogk%C3%B6z&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bodrogköz (page does not exist)">Bodrogköz</a> suggested to be a population isolate found an elevated frequency of Haplogroup N: R1a-M458 (20.4%), I2a1-P37 (19%), R1a-Z280 (14.3%), and E1b-M78 (10.2%). Various R1b-M343 subgroups accounted for 15% of the Bodrogköz population. Haplogroup N1c-Tat covered 6.2% of the lineages, but most of it belonged to the N1c-VL29 subgroup, which is more frequent among <a href="/wiki/Balto-Slavic_languages" title="Balto-Slavic languages">Balto-Slavic</a> speaking than Finno-Ugric speaking peoples. Other haplogroups had frequencies of less than 5%.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Among 100 Hungarian men, 90 of whom from the <a href="/wiki/Great_Hungarian_Plain" title="Great Hungarian Plain">Great Hungarian Plain</a>, the following haplogroups and frequencies are obtained: 30% R1a, 15% R1b, 13% I2a1, 13% J2, 9% E1b1b1a, 8% I1, 3% G2, 3% J1, 3% I*, 1% E*, 1% F*, 1% K*. The 97 <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9kelys" title="Székelys">Székelys</a> belong to the following haplogroups: 20% R1b, 19% R1a, 17% I1, 11% J2, 10% J1, 8% E1b1b1a, 5% I2a1, 5% G2, 3% P*, 1% E*, 1% N.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> It can be inferred that Szekelys have more significant German admixture. A study sampling 45 <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%B3c" title="Palóc">Palóc</a> from Budapest and northern Hungary, found 60% R1a, 13% R1b, 11% I, 9% E, 2% G, 2% J2.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>  A study estimating possible Inner Asian admixture among nearly 500 Hungarians based on paternal lineages only, estimated it at 5.1% in Hungary, at 7.4 in <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9kelys" title="Székelys">Székelys</a> and at 6.3% at <a href="/wiki/Csangos" title="Csangos">Csangos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> It has boldly been noted that this is an upper limit by deep SNPs and that the main haplogroups responsible for that contribution are J2-M172 (negative M47, M67, L24, M12), J2-L24, R1a-Z93, Q-M242 and E-M78, the latter of which is typically European, while N is still negligible (1.7%). In an attempt to divide N into subgroups L1034 and L708, some Hungarian, <a href="/wiki/Sz%C3%A9kely" class="mw-redirect" title="Székely">Székely</a>, and Uzbek samples were found to be L1034 SNP positive, while all Mongolians, <a href="/wiki/Buryats" title="Buryats">Buryats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khanty_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Khanty people">Khanty</a>, Finnish, and Roma samples showed a negative result for this marker. The 2500 years old SNP L1034 was found typical for <a href="/wiki/Mansi_people" title="Mansi people">Mansi</a> and Hungarians, the closest linguistic relatives.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The following information is inferred from 433 Hungarian samples from the Hungarian Magyar Y-DNA Project in <a href="/wiki/Family_Tree" class="mw-redirect" title="Family Tree">Family Tree</a> (29 May 2017):<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>26.1% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_R1a" title="Haplogroup R1a">R1a</a> (15% Z280, 6.5% M458, 0.9% Z93=&gt;S23201 "<a href="/wiki/Altai_people" title="Altai people">Altai</a>/<a href="/wiki/Tian_Shan" title="Tian Shan">Tian Shan</a>", 3.7% unknown)</li>
<li>19.2% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_R1b" title="Haplogroup R1b">R1b</a> (6% L11-P312/U106, 5.3% P312, 4.2% L23/Z2103, 3.7% U106)</li>
<li>16.9% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_I-M438" title="Haplogroup I-M438">I2</a> (15.2% CTS10228, 1.4% M223, 0.5% L38)</li>
<li>8.3% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_I1" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup I1">I1</a></li>
<li>8.1% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_J2" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup J2">J2</a> (5.3% M410, 2.8% M102)</li>
<li>6.9% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_E-M35" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup E-M35">E1b1b1</a> (6% V13, 0.3% V22, 0.3% M123, 0.3% M81)</li>
<li>6.9% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_G2a" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup G2a">G2a</a></li>
<li>3.2% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_N-M231" title="Haplogroup N-M231">N</a> (1.4% Z9136 "Ugric/Proto-Magyar", 0.5% M2019/VL67 "Siberia and Baykal", 0.5% Y7310 "Central Europe", 0.9% Z16981 "Baltic")- note: only unrelated males are sampled</li>
<li>2.3% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_Q_(Y-DNA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup Q (Y-DNA)">Q</a> (1.2% YP789 "Huns/Turkmens", 0.9% M346 "Siberia", 0.2% M242 "<a href="/wiki/Xiongnu#Genetics" title="Xiongnu">Xiongnu</a>")</li>
<li>0.9% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_T_(Y-DNA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup T (Y-DNA)">T</a></li>
<li>0.5% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_J1" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup J1">J1</a></li>
<li>0.2% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_L_(Y-DNA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup L (Y-DNA)">L</a></li>
<li>0.2% <a href="/wiki/Haplogroup_C_(Y-DNA)" class="mw-redirect" title="Haplogroup C (Y-DNA)">C</a></li></ul>

</div>
</div>
<p>Besides the various peoples mentioned above, the Magyars later assimilated or were influenced by other populations in the Carpathian Basin. Among these are the <a href="/wiki/Cumans" title="Cumans">Cumans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pechenegs" title="Pechenegs">Pechenegs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jasz_people" title="Jasz people">Jazones</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Slavs" title="West Slavs">West Slavs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vlachs" title="Vlachs">Vlachs</a> (<a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a>), amongst others. <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a>, who occupied the central part of Hungary from c. 1526 until c. 1699, inevitably exerted an influence, as did the various nations (Germans, Slovaks, Serbs, Croats, and others) that resettled depopulated territories after their departure. Similar to other European countries, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Hungary" title="History of the Jews in Hungary">Jewish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Armenians" title="Armenians">Armenians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">Roma</a> (Gypsy) minorities have been living in Hungary since the Middle Ages.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungarian_diaspora">Hungarian diaspora</span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_diaspora" title="Hungarian diaspora">Hungarian diaspora</a></div>
<p>Hungarian diaspora (Magyar diaspora) is a term that encompasses the total ethnic Hungarian population located outside of current-day Hungary.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r905231330">.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery{display:table}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-default{background:transparent;margin-top:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-center{margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-left{float:left}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-right{float:right}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-none{float:none}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-collapsible{width:100%}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .title,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .main,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .footer{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .title>div{display:table-cell;text-align:center;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .main>div{display:table-cell}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .caption{display:table-row;vertical-align:top}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .caption>div{display:table-cell;display:block;font-size:94%;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .footer>div{display:table-cell;text-align:right;font-size:80%;line-height:1em}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .gallerybox .thumb img{background:none}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .bordered-images img{border:solid #eee 1px}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .whitebg img,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .gallerybox div{background:#fff!important}</style><div class="mod-gallery mod-gallery-default mod-gallery-center"><div class="title"><div>Maps of the Hungarian diaspora</div></div><div class="main"><div><ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional nochecker bordered-images" style="line-height:130%;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Maps">Maps</span></h2>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:36px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ethnic_map_of_11th_century.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ethnic_map_of_11th_century.jpg/120px-Ethnic_map_of_11th_century.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="78" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ethnic_map_of_11th_century.jpg/180px-Ethnic_map_of_11th_century.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Ethnic_map_of_11th_century.jpg/240px-Ethnic_map_of_11th_century.jpg 2x" data-file-width="806" data-file-height="526" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>Kniezsa's (1938) view on the ethnic map of the Kingdom of Hungary in the 11th century, based on <a href="/wiki/Toponyms" class="mw-redirect" title="Toponyms">toponyms</a>. Kniezsa's view has been criticized by many scholars, because of its non-compliance with later archaeological and onomastics research, but his map is still regularly cited in modern reliable sources.<sup style="white-space:nowrap;font-style:italic;">[under <a href="/wiki/Talk:Hungarians#Kniezsa&#39;s_ethnic_map" title="Talk:Hungarians">discussion</a>]</sup>
</p>

<p>The "Red Map"<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Your explanation here (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, based on the controversial 1910 census (peak of the <a href="/wiki/Magyarization" title="Magyarization">magyarization</a>): Hungarians in the Kingdom of Hungary
</p>
			</div>

		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">

<li id="cite_note-Bálint-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Bálint_54-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Bálint_54-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Bálint_54-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal">Csanád Bálint (October 2008). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.matud.iif.hu/08okt/02.html">"A történeti genetika és az eredetkérdés(ek)"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Magyar_Tudom%C3%A1ny" title="Magyar Tudomány">Magyar Tudomány</a></i>: 1170<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">6 October</span> 2009</span>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=Magyar+Tudom%C3%A1ny&amp;rft.atitle=A+t%C3%B6rt%C3%A9neti+genetika+%C3%A9s+az+eredetk%C3%A9rd%C3%A9s%28ek%29&amp;rft.pages=1170&amp;rft.date=2008-10&amp;rft.au=Csan%C3%A1d+B%C3%A1lint&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.matud.iif.hu%2F08okt%2F02.html&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AHungarians" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/> <i>Cited:</i> "Lipták Pálnak köszönhetően közel fél évszázada tudjuk, hogy a 10. sz.-i embercsontoknak csak 16,7&#160;%-a tartozik a mongolid és az europo-mongolid rasszhoz. Tehát a mai magyarság szerológiai, és genetikai összetételében egyértelműen kimutatott európai jelleg, ugyanakkor az ázsiainak hiánya nem egyedül az eltelt ezer év keveredéseinek köszönhető, hanem már a honfoglalás- és Szent István-kori Magyarország lakossága is szinte kizárólag biológiailag európai eredetűekből állt." <i>Translation:</i> "Due to Pál Lipták we have known for almost half a century that only 16.7 percent of 10th-century human bones belong to the Euro-Mongoloid and Mongoloid races. Thus, the unambiguously established European characteristics in the genetic and serological composition of the recent Hungarian population and the lack of Asian markers are not solely due to the thousand years of blending but biologically the populations of the conquest period and of St Stephen's Hungary were made up almost exclusively of peoples of European origin."</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-55">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pál Lipták: A magyarság etnogenezisének paleoantropológiája (The paleoanthropology of Hungarian people's ethnogenesis) (Antropológiai Közl., 1970. 14. sz.)</span>

<li id="cite_note-66"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-66">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Science, 14 February 2014, Vol. 343 no. 6172, p. 751, A Genetic Atlas of Human Admixture History, Garrett Hellenthal at al.: "CIs. for the admixture time(s) overlap but predate the Mongol empire, with estimates from 440 to 1080 CE (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC4209567/figure/F3/">Fig.3.</a>) In each population, one source group has at least some ancestry related to Northeast Asians, with ~2 to 4% of these groups total ancestry linking directly to East Asia. This signal might correspond to a small genetic legacy from invasions of peoples from the Asian steppes (e.g., the Huns, Magyars, and Bulgars) during the first millennium CE."</span>

<li><a href="/wiki/K%C3%A1roly_Kocsis" title="Károly Kocsis">Károly Kocsis</a> (<a href="/wiki/DSc" class="mw-redirect" title="DSc">DSc</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Miskolc" title="University of Miskolc">University of Miskolc</a>) – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Zsolt_Bottlik&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zsolt Bottlik (page does not exist)">Zsolt Bottlik</a> (PhD, <a href="/wiki/Budapest_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Budapest University">Budapest University</a>) – <a href="/w/index.php?title=Patrik_T%C3%A1trai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Patrik Tátrai (page does not exist)">Patrik Tátrai</a>: Etnikai térfolyamatok a Kárpát-medence határon túli régióiban + CD (for detailed data), Magyar Tudományos Akadémia (<a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Hungarian Academy of Sciences">Hungarian Academy of Sciences</a>) – Földrajtudományi Kutatóintézet (Academy of Geographical Studies); Budapest; 2006.; <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886058088"/><a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/963-9545-10-4" title="Special:BookSources/963-9545-10-4">963-9545-10-4</a></li></ul>
